Rain McKenzie</name>
<Time>1505803935106<//Time><Rating>3< /Rating>< review>
Wonderful grounds to walk around on but there are homeless people sleeping and hanging out all day long here. I come here about four times a year with friends and family and have hosted a couple get together/events here. The homeless people sleep under the trees for the shade in the summer and crowd the benches near some of the sculptures. When it rains they sleep under the shelter where the doors are up at the building. On one occasion when I came here with some out-of-town friends a homeless man was bathing himself at the Rock fountain near the trellis and stairs. This is one of the nicest sculpture parks in the area so I keep coming back. It would just be nice if there weren't so many vagrants loitering around and pissing on the trees.< /review>

< text>
Great care, but they're constantly trying to add on unnecessary checks and products. I felt like I was at one of those vacation program seminars.
UPDATE!!!

So after their comment below and six months have passed, I felt the need to update this review and provide a deeper story.

We started using this vet 12 years ago when we lived nearby.  Five years later, we moved to South Carolina and had a clean break. They willingly and easily transferred our dog's record to the new vet and we never heard from them again. During the time we were with them, the service was great. Super friendly and very professional. Not cheap by any standard, but we didn't want cheap, we wanted quality, so that was ok.

Two years after we left CA, we moved back, but to San Diego. While we were in South Carolina, our dog developed epilepsy and required medication plus blood work every six months, so vet visits became quite regular.

During a one week visit back in Folsom, our dog was attacked by an animal. We had her cleaned up and checked out by an emergency vet, but then went back to this place for two follow up appointments before going back home.

At both visits, I was asked many unnecessary questions at the desk, then in the exam room by the assistant, and then again by the vet in the exam room.  Despite letting them know over the phone when I made the appointments, and in person to all three people asking the questions that we were only there to check her wound, I was still asked the full gamut each time.

They were essentially helping me change a bandaid and check for infection. And yet they were trying to tell me that she was behind on all her shots. They tried to find out what diet I had her on. They conducted and charged me for a full blown exam. It didn't matter when I told them that she sees another vet every 6 months, we don't live near them, and their records are not accurate. Both times I came in I had to fight my way out to avoid extra costs.

For the last 6 months, I've been getting monthly reminders in the mail that our dog is overdue for an exam. Why in the world would they send a flyer to an address that's over 500 miles away?

To further solidify their hard selling techniques, just take a look around their office if you find yourself in it. There isn't one square foot of wall space that isn't covered with something that you should buy if you care about your pet.

This is in stark contrast to what my San Diego vet office is like. They have one shelf of special food that they sell, and that's in the corner behind the desk. Every other wall is just either sparsely decorated or filled with pictures of clients' pets. I don't even get reminders in the mail to remind me when my dog's due for her checkup. Conveniently, this happens when her bottle of medication runs out.

I updated this because my wife finally got fed up with the spam mail and called them to make sure the pestering stops. If it doesn't, be assured that I'll update this review again.< /text>

It is now March 2017, and I just had my second surgery to fix things that could have avoided in the first place if he did the surgery right. A week after I had my wisdom teeth taken out, I got an infection so I was put on a small dose of antibiotic by Slaughter. A week or so later I had finished the antibiotic and left the country for a vacation. My first night in Belize, I woke up and the infection had gotten very bad. That morning I went to a doctor in the nearest town and he had to squeeze the infection out with his hands because it was so bad. He then put me on a stronger antibiotic (what Slaughter should have put me on in the first place) and it killed most of the infection. When I got back home, I went back to Slaughter and he found a piece of dead bone that he left in. He thought nothing of it.

Yesterday, March 24th I had a biopsy and they found a piece of root from my wisdom tooth that had been left in there!!! It was causing a serious infection to where my bone was very soft and mushy.

< review>
I hope Dr. WILSON and his staff read this !!!!

I think Dr. WILSON is one of the best doctors/dentists who has ever treated me in my entire lifetime and I will b 66 on 11/11/2018. He does not act so busy as if I am wasting his precious time. I happen to know that this is quite rare for medical professionals these days because approx. 2 weeks after my oral surgery w/ Wilson I had another surgery & this surgeon moved, talked & reacted so quickly that it made me nervous & uncomfortable & scared. This surgeon had a much larger support team but somehow I felt like I was just another patient in a long line of scheduled surgeries. Dr. Wilson called me himself and also one of his staff following my procedure to "check in on me ". WOW ! THAT IS A VERY KIND & CONSIDERATE THING TO DO. OF COARSE NO PHONE CALL FROM THE OTHER SURGEON NOR ANY OF HIS STAFF. The pre-op instructions from the other surgeon included 4 simple things: 1. Hav responsible adult pick up after surgery. 2. But nothing about not eating/drinking b4 procedure which I knew I had to do from Dr. WILSON'S PRE-OP INSTRUCTIONS. This last visit though, I ordered the usual 4 subs and when I brought them home I was so disappointed and upset that the subs were loaded with nothing but onion. <Time>1450421172945< /Time>< Text>
Very highly recommended. This location is "new" - that is, although the buildings have been here for some time, the property has only just recently become part of the Extra Space brand...and they've done a thorough facelift on the place. I've been to a number of self storage places over the years, including some other ExtraSpace locations, and they always feel vaguely horror-movie-ish...long,  scary hallways with flickering light bulbs, rusty elevators and creaky doors. Not so at this place. SUPER clean, well-lit hallways inside AND plenty of floodlights outside, and freshly painted. Units are odor free, individually alarmed, and well lit  also.

My only suggestion is adding doorstops at the hallway entrances, and smoothing out the transitions from the ground outside to the concrete floor of the hallways...as it is, the slight lip of the concrete sometimes makes it difficult to roll a hand truck through the door.

Keep it up!</Text>
